The Impossibility of Reports about the Impossible
Baqillani describes the impossible report and its necessary falsehood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's definition of a report about the impossible, why it is necessarily false, and from whom such a report cannot originate.

Core Idea
Reports about the impossible are always false and cannot come from truthful sources.

Baqillani continues his classification of reports by turning to those that convey impossible content. He explains that impossibility is determined either by direct sense perception or by rational proofs. Such reports are always false, and they can never be uttered by God, prophets, or reliable transmitters. This lesson examines the reasoning behind these claims and clarifies common misunderstandings about miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once without overthinking, then read the translation. Focus on the definition of the second type of report and the examples given.
Notice how Baqillani distinguishes between impossibility based on senses and impossibility based on proofs.
2
Identify the criteria for impossibility
The passage lists two ways impossibility is established: by the judgment of the senses/necessities, or by proofs and evidences. Find these and understand the distinction.
3
Examine the examples
Look at the examples: reporting non-existence of what we see, claiming something contrary to sensory perception, reporting events like the dead rising or a staff turning into a snake in our time, and logical impossibilities like two opposites in one locus.
These examples illustrate what is meant by 'impossible' in the context of reports.
4
Understand the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that such a report is always false and cannot come from God (al-Qadīm), a prophet, someone prophesied to be truthful, or a group that establishes tawātur. Ask yourself why this is so.
The key reason is that lying is impermissible for these sources, and the report's content is known to be false.
5
Address the common misunderstanding
Many people confuse reports about the impossible with miraculous reports. Reflect on how Baqillani's definition of impossibility is tied to normal custom and reason, leaving room for divine miracles that transcend custom.
The passage does not deny miracles; it only denies that a report contrary to established custom can be true if it is presented as a normal occurrence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والضرب الثاني خَبَرٌ عن محال ممتنع إما بقضية الحواس والضرورات أو بما قام عليه من الحجج والدلالات نحو الخبر عن عدم ما نشاهده وكونه على خلاف صفة ما ندركه عليه والخبر عن قيام الأموات وقلب العصا حيةً وانقلاب دجلة ذهباً في وقتنا هذا والخبر عن وجود الضدين في محل واحد وكون الجسم في مكانين وما جرى مَجْرَى ذلك من المحال المعلوم بطلانه بقضايا الحواس وموضوع العادات وأوائل العقول والضرورات. وهذا الخبر لا يقع أبداً إلا كذباً ممن وقع منه لثبوت العلم ببطلان مُخبره وتناوله له على غير ما هو به. وليس يجوز أن يقع هذا الخبر من القديم ولا من نبي ولا ممن نُبئ عنه أنه لا يكذب ولا من قوم يثبت بهم التواتر ويُعلم صدقهم اضطراراً إذا نقلوا عن مشاهدة من غير قهر وإجبار وأسباب يظهر عليهم الحديث بها لأن الكذب لا يجوز على من ذكرناه فيما هذه حاله.
And the second type is a report about the impossible (muḥāl mumtaniʿ), either by the judgment of the senses and necessities, or by what has been established of proofs and evidences, such as the report about the non-existence of what we witness and its being contrary to the quality we perceive it upon, and the report about the rising of the dead, the turning of the staff into a snake, and the turning of the Tigris into gold in our time, and the report about the existence of two opposites in one locus and the body being in two places, and whatever runs along that course of the impossible whose falsehood is known by the judgments of the senses, the subject of customs, the first principles of the intellects, and necessities. And this report never occurs except as falsehood from whomever it occurs, due to the establishment of knowledge of the falsehood of its content and its taking of it in other than what it is. And it is not permissible that this report occur from the Eternal, nor from a prophet, nor from one who is prophesied about that he does not lie, nor from a people by whom tawātur is established and their truth is known necessarily when they transmit from direct observation without coercion, compulsion, or causes that appear upon them of discourse, because lying is not permissible upon those whom we have mentioned in this state.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage explains the second type of report: a report about what is impossible (muḥāl mumtaniʿ). Such impossibility is determined either by direct sense perception and necessities or by proofs and evidences. The author gives examples: reporting the non-existence of something we directly witness, reporting something contrary to our perception (like saying the dead have risen or a staff turned into a snake in our present time), reporting the coexistence of opposites or a body in two places simultaneously. These reports are necessarily false because their content is known to be false. Furthermore, such reports cannot possibly come from certain sources: from God (al-Qadīm), from a prophet, from someone about whom it is prophesied that they do not lie (implying a truthful messenger), or from a group that constitutes tawātur (mass transmission) — since such groups are known to be truthful when they report from direct observation without coercion. The reasoning is that lying is not permissible for these individuals or groups, given their established truthfulness. Thus, if someone reports something impossible, we know they are lying, and the report cannot be from a reliable source.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think a report about a miracle is impossible; but Baqillani clarifies that impossibility is judged by normal course of events, and miracles are possible through divine intervention.
Correction: The impossibility here refers to what is contrary to established custom and reason, not to divine acts which are beyond custom.

Checkpoint

A) From a liar
B) From an ignorant person
C) From a prophet
D) From a common person

Key Takeaway
Reports about the impossible are always false by rational necessity and do not occur from truthful sources.

?

Will you re-evaluate that belief today?
?
Consider your own speech: have you ever reported something you knew was false or exaggerated? Baqillani says that reports about the impossible are always lies. What about reports that stretch the truth? Are you truthful in your reports? What steps will you take to ensure your words are always truthful, even when it costs you?
?
The passage says that even God and prophets do not report impossibilities. If the most truthful sources never lie, what does that say about your own responsibility to speak only the truth? Are there areas in your life where you have compromised truthfulness? What will you change today to align your speech with the truth that God demands?

Proof of Tawatur: Impossibility of Lying by the Mass Transmitters
Baqillani provides a proof for the impossibility of lying by a tawatur-sized group

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that a tawatur-sized group cannot lie, based on customary experience (adah) and the analogy of collective self-mutilation.

Core Idea
Custom prevents a large group from conspiring to lie, just as it prevents mass self-mutilation.

Baqillani addresses a key objection to tawatur: How can we be sure that a large group of transmitters did not collude to fabricate a report? He argues that human custom (adah) makes such collusion impossible, especially when the report concerns witnessed events. This lesson unpacks his proof, including a vivid analogy that drives the point home.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the objection and the beginning of the answer.
The passage is a single long sentence; break it into parts.
2
Identify the objection and the answer
Find the question: 'What is the evidence...?' and then how Baqillani responds by recalling the earlier point about the miracles of the messengers.
3
Understand the role of custom (adah)
Baqillani argues that custom does not allow a large group to agree on a lie about a witnessed event, nor to conceal it. Consider why this is a strong argument.
Contrast with the possibility for one or two individuals.
4
Analyze the analogy
Baqillani compares lying to collective self-mutilation—just as a large group cannot agree to disfigure themselves, they cannot agree to lie in tawatur reports.
This analogy highlights the practical impossibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إثبات التواتر واستحالة الكذب على أهله إن قال قائل : ما الدليل على استحالة الكذب على العدد الذين يثبت بهم التواتر؟ قيل له : ما قدمنا عند القول في نقل أعلام الرسل وهو أن العادة لم تجر باجتماع مثل عدد أهل التواتر على نقل كذب عن مشاهدة ولا على كتمان ما هم عالمون به غير ظهور الحديث به بينهم والإقرار إذا خلوا، بأنهم كتموا وتشاعروا لعلة دعتهم إلى ذلك لأنه لا يجوز أن يستمر ترك ذلك والخوض فيه والحديث به زماناً طويلاً أو الأبد حتى حالهم أنهم قد افتعلوا وإن جاز ذلك على الواحد والاثنين منهم كما أنه لم تجر العادة باجتماع مثلهم على التشويه بأنفسهم والتعالج لتشويه وجوههم وكشف سواتهم وعوراتهم وطلاق نسائهم، والخروج بهم في
Chapter on Discourse concerning Establishing Tawatur and the Impossibility of Lying upon Its People. If someone says: What is the evidence for the impossibility of lying upon the number by which tawatur is established? It is said to him: That which we presented earlier when discussing the transmission of the signs of the messengers – namely that custom does not allow that a group of the size of the people of tawatur should congregate upon transmitting a lie from direct observation, nor upon concealing what they know, without the report becoming public among them and their confessing, when they are alone, that they concealed and colluded for a reason that prompted them to that. For it is not possible that they should continue to abandon that, engage in it, and speak about it for a long time or forever, such that their state would be that they fabricated it, even if that is possible for one or two of them. Just as custom does not allow that a group of their like should congregate upon disfiguring themselves, treating themselves to disfigure their faces, exposing their private parts and shameful areas, divorcing their wives, and going out with them
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the impossibility of lying by a group that meets the conditions of tawatur (mass transmission). It begins with an objection: 'What is the evidence that lying is impossible for the number of people who establish tawatur?' The answer recalls an earlier point about the transmission of the miracles of the messengers. The core argument is based on 'adah (customary experience). Custom does not allow that such a large group would collectively agree (ijtima') to transmit a lie about something they claim to have witnessed directly, nor would they all agree to conceal what they know. If they were lying, it would be impossible for them to maintain the secret over a long period without the truth emerging. Moreover, when they are alone, they would confess that they fabricated it. This is analogous to the impossibility of a large group agreeing to harm themselves collectively (e.g., disfiguring their faces, exposing their private parts, divorcing their wives). While one or two individuals might do such things, a large group cannot maintain such extraordinary behavior. Thus, the tawatur report must be true.

Key Terms
التواتر
استحالة الكذب
العادة
العدد
النقل عن مشاهدة
التشويه
التعالج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that large groups can lie with impunity, especially if they coordinate.
Correction: Baqillani argues that customary experience (adah) prevents a tawatur-sized group from successfully fabricating a report about witnessed events, because such a conspiracy would inevitably unravel.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Baqillani use to prove that a tawatur-sized group cannot lie about a witnessed event?
A) The impossibility of a group agreeing to eat together.
B) The impossibility of a group agreeing to disfigure themselves collectively.
C) The impossibility of a group agreeing to travel together.
D) The impossibility of a group agreeing to remain silent.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani proves tawatur by arguing that custom renders large-scale conspiracy to lie impossible, just as it prevents collective self-harm.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a widely reported piece of news, do you automatically assume it's true because 'everyone says so'? How does Baqillani's condition that the transmitters must have directly observed what they report challenge your default trust in mass reports? Where in your life have you accepted something on hearsay without verifying the source?
?
Baqillani says that if a group lied, they would eventually confess when alone. Think of a secret you have kept as part of a group. Why haven't you confessed it? Are you afraid of consequences, or is it because deep down you know the truth will eventually come out? How does this passage force you to confront your own hidden collusions?
?
What one belief about Islam do you hold that ultimately rests on tawatur (e.g., the Quran's preservation, the story of the Prophet's life)? After understanding Baqillani's argument, are you more certain or less certain of that belief? What action will you take today to reinforce that certainty or to investigate it further?

Baqillani's Proof of the Impossibility of Lying for a Tawatur Group
Baqillani proves impossibility of lying for the tawatur group through a proof by custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that a tawatur group cannot collude on a lie because custom ('adah) and conflicting human motives make such sustained deception impossible.

Core Idea
Custom prevents a large group from lying just as it prevents collective self-mutilation.

In this lesson, we engage directly with a key passage from Imam Baqillani's Tamhid. He defends the reliability of tawatur (consecutive transmission) by proving that it is impossible for a sufficiently large group to conspire on a false report. Using an analogy to extreme physical acts, he shows that custom and divergent human motives preclude such collusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and Translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the question-answer format: an objector asks for evidence, and Baqillani responds.
2
Identify the Core Argument
Find where Baqillani states that custom does not allow a tawatur group to transmit a lie from observation or to conceal the truth. Notice how he says it is 'not permissible' for them to persist in falsehood forever.
The argument relies on custom ('adah), not logical necessity.
3
Analyze the Analogy
Read the analogy about self-mutilation, divorce, and travel. Ask yourself: how does comparing lying to these extreme acts strengthen the proof?
The analogy shows that just as people cannot all agree to harm themselves, they cannot all agree to lie persistently.
4
Reflect on the Conclusion
Consider Baqillani's statement that whoever allows the group to lie because individuals can is like allowing them to collectively self-mutilate. Why is this a powerful rebuttal?
This highlights the difference between individual possibility and collective impossibility by custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في إثبات التواتر واستحالة الكذب على أهله. إن قال قائل: ما الدليل على استحالة الكذب على العدد الذين يثبت بهم التواتر؟ قيل له: ما قدمنا عند القول في نقل أعلام الرسل وهو أن العادة لم تجر باجتماع مثل عدد أهل التواتر على نقل كذب عن مشاهدة ولا على كتمان ما هم عالمون به غير ظهور الحديث به بينهم والإقرار إذا خلوا، بأنهم كتموا وتشاعروا لعلة دعتهم إلى ذلك لأنه لا يجوز أن يستمر ترك ذلك والخوض فيه والحديث به زماناً طويلاً أو الأبد حتى حالهم أنهم قد افتعلوا وإن جاز ذلك على الواحد والاثنين منهم كما أنه لم تجر العادة باجتماع مثلهم على التشويه بأنفسهم والتعالج لتشويه وجوههم وكشف سواتهم وعوراتهم وطلاق نسائهم، والخروج بهم من ديارهم وشخوص أجمعهم إلى بلد كرمان وشيراز وبلد الصين واحتمال هول البحر وغير ذلك من المتاجر والصنائع لما جعلهم الله عليه من تفرق الدواعي واختلاف الهمم والأعراض فمن أراد أن يجيز الكذب على جميعهم عند الاجتماع لجواز ذلك على آحادهم عند الانفراد، فهو كمن جوز عليهم جميع الذي وصفنا مع اجتماعهم لجواز ذلك على آحادهم عند الانفراد وكل ذلك محال معلوم امتناعه وتعذره في العادة.
Chapter on establishing tawatur (consecutive transmission) and the impossibility of lying upon its people. If a questioner says: What is the evidence for the impossibility of lying upon the number of people by whom tawatur is established? It is said to him: What we have presented earlier in the discussion on the transmission of the signs of the messengers, namely that custom has not run by the coming together of a number like the number of the people of tawatur upon transmitting a lie from direct observation, nor upon concealing what they are knowledgeable about, not appearing of the narration among them, and admission when they are alone, that they concealed it and conspired for a reason that called them to that, because it is not permissible that the abandonment of that, engaging in it, and speaking about it should continue for a long time or forever, until their state is that they have fabricated it, even if that is permissible upon one or two of them. Just as custom has not run by the coming together of their likes upon disfiguring themselves and treating to disfigure their faces, exposing their private parts and genitals, divorcing their wives, and going out from their homes, all of them journeying to a city like Kirman, Shiraz, the land of China, enduring the terror of the sea and other such things of trade and crafts, because of what God has placed them upon of dispersal of motives and difference of intentions and desires. So whoever wants to permit lying upon all of them when gathered together due to permissibility of that upon individuals when alone, he is like one who permits upon all of them all what we described with their gathering for the permissibility of that upon individuals when alone. And all of that is impossible, known impossibility and difficulty in custom.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a proof. It begins by opening a chapter on establishing tawatur and the impossibility of lying for its transmitters. The author then presents an objection: 'What is the evidence that lying is impossible for the group that reaches the level of tawatur?' The answer is a reference to a previous discussion about 'the transmission of the signs of the messengers.' The core argument is that custom ('adah) does not allow such a large group to agree upon a lie from direct observation, nor to conceal what they know, without the report appearing among them and without them admitting to concealment when alone. The reason is that it is impossible for them to continue this concealment and silence indefinitely; eventually their condition would reveal that they fabricated it. This is contrasted with the possibility of a lie by one or two individuals. The author then provides a striking analogy: just as custom does not allow a large group to collude in acts like disfiguring themselves, exposing their private parts, divorcing their wives, or undertaking arduous journeys to distant lands for trade—due to the natural dispersion of motives and interests—so too it does not allow collective deception. Therefore, someone who claims that a lie is possible for the entire group merely because it is possible for individuals is like someone who claims that the group could do all those extreme acts just because individuals could. All of that is known to be impossible by custom.

Key Terms
تواتر
استحالة الكذب
العادة
أهل التواتر
تشويه
اضطرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Because individuals can lie, a large group can also lie collectively.
Correction: Baqillani argues that while lying is possible for one or two, custom makes it impossible for a large group to collude on a lie persistently, due to divergent motives. The analogy with self-harm shows that individual possibility does not imply group possibility.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence that a tawatur group cannot conspire to lie?
A) The group members are all righteous and incapable of lying.
B) Custom (adah) does not allow such a large group to persist in lying forever without exposure, just as it prevents them from jointly self-mutilating.
C) The report is always accompanied by miracles.
D) The group is too large to agree on anything.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's proof shows that the impossibility of a tawatur group lying is known by custom, not by logical necessity but as a customary certainty grounded in human nature and experience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are part of a group that shares a false narrative, do you remain silent or speak the truth? What does this lesson say about the impossibility of a group maintaining a lie forever?
?
This proof relies on custom and human nature. In your own life, have you ever witnessed a group cover-up that eventually unraveled? How does that experience affirm or challenge Baqillani's argument?
?
If custom prevents a large group from lying, what does that imply about your own responsibility to be truthful even when alone? Are you relying on the custom of others to maintain truth, or are you personally committed to truth?

Baqillani's Proof that Knowledge from Tawatur is Necessary
Baqillani proves that knowledge from tawatur is necessarily acquired by direct experience.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that knowledge from tawatur is necessary (daruri) because it is felt as certain as sensory knowledge and shared by all people including non-specialists.

Core Idea
Knowledge from tawatur is as immediate and undeniable as seeing with your own eyes.

Baqillani anticipates a critical objection: how do we know that knowledge from tawatur is necessary? He answers with two powerful observations. First, we experience such knowledge with the same immediacy and certainty as sensory perception. Second, this knowledge is not limited to scholars but is shared even by women, common folk, and detractors who lack theoretical reasoning. This passage establishes the epistemological foundation for relying on tawatur as a source of certain knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Start by reading the objection and the first part of Baqillani's answer. Notice how he compares knowledge from tawatur to sensory and introspective knowledge.
The objection sets up the question: what proves that this knowledge is necessary?
2
Examine the second argument
Read the second argument about women, common people, and disparagers. Ask yourself why their involvement proves necessity.
This argument appeals to universality—if only scholars had it, it might be acquired through reasoning.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
See how both arguments together establish that the knowledge is necessary. Reflect on why this matters for Islamic theology.
Necessary knowledge is indubitable and does not require further proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل: ما الدليل على أن العلم بمخبر خبر من ذكرتم يقع اضطراراً؟ قيل له: الدليل على ذلك أننا نجد أنفسنا عالمة بما يخبرون عنه على حد ما نجدها عالمة بما تدركه من حواسنا وما نجده من أنفسنا مما لا يمكننا الشك فيه ولأنه قد شاركنا في العلم به النساء والعامة والمتنقصون الذين ليسوا من أهل النظر فثبت أن العلم بذلك ضرورة على ما قلناه.
Then if a questioner says: What is the evidence that knowledge of the reported content of the report of those you mentioned occurs necessarily? It is said to him: The evidence for that is that we find ourselves knowing what they report about just as we find ourselves knowing what we perceive from our senses and what we find from ourselves that we cannot doubt. And because women, the common people, and the disparagers who are not people of reflection have shared in this knowledge with us. So it is established that knowledge of that is necessary as we said.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a proof in the form of an objection and answer. The questioner asks: 'What is the evidence that knowledge of the content of a report from the tawatur group you mentioned occurs necessarily?' The answer provides two arguments. First, we find ourselves knowing what they report just as we find ourselves knowing what we perceive through our senses and what we find within ourselves that is beyond doubt. This suggests that this knowledge is as immediate and unavoidable as sensory or introspective knowledge. Second, this knowledge is shared not only by reflective scholars but also by women, the common people, and even those who belittle the reports—people who are not capable of theoretical reasoning. This universality indicates that such knowledge does not depend on reflection but is necessary (daruri). Therefore, it is established that knowledge from tawatur is indeed necessary, as claimed.

Key Terms
العلم الضروري
اضطرار
خبر التواتر
الحواس
النظر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Knowledge from tawatur is acquired through theoretical reasoning or scholarly investigation.
Correction: Baqillani shows that this knowledge is immediate and undeniable, and is possessed even by those incapable of reasoning, so it must be necessary, not acquired.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani argue that knowledge from tawatur is necessary?
A) Because it is derived from logical deduction.
B) Because it is shared by women and the common people, and felt as certain as sensory knowledge.
C) Because the transmitters are all trustworthy.
D) Because the report is recorded in scripture.

Key Takeaway
Knowledge from tawatur is necessary because it is experienced as certain and shared by all people, including those incapable of reasoning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a widely transmitted report about Islam that you have not personally verified, do you treat it with the same certainty as you treat your own senses? What stops you from doing so, and what would Baqillani say about that hesitation?
?
Consider a piece of knowledge from tawatur that even those who mock Islam possess, such as the existence of Mecca. If that knowledge is necessary and undeniable, what excuse do you have for not acting on it?
?
Is there any report from tawatur that you have doubted or dismissed? If so, how does Baqillani's argument that such knowledge is as certain as your own hunger challenge your doubt, and what will you do about it today?
